## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem of determining rate laws in chemical kinetics. The relationship likely follows standard rate law forms (nth-order kinetics, reversible reactions, or more complex mechanisms).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of single species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (product-catalyzed reaction)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction)
- Time-dependent forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent rate coefficient)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with equilibrium shift)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding)
- Exponential decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * A) (concentration-dependent activation energy)
- Polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 + c2 * A**3 (complex mechanism expansion)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration raised to integer power → elementary reaction step with molecularity equal to that integer (mass action kinetics)
- Rate proportional to A*(constant - A) → logistic/autocatalytic behavior where product catalyzes the reaction
- Rational function of concentration (A/(K+A)) → enzyme saturation or surface adsorption limiting step
- Sum of terms with different powers of A → parallel reaction pathways or competing mechanisms
- Negative constant term added to rate expression → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium concentration
- Rate expression with A in denominator squared → substrate/product inhibition mechanism
- Explicit time dependence multiplied by concentration → photochemical reaction with varying light intensity or catalyst deactivation
- Exponential function of concentration → non-Arrhenius effects or activity coefficient corrections in concentrated solutions
- Square root of concentration (A**0.5) → dissociative adsorption or radical chain mechanism with termination
